text:
This recipe is awesome! My family loved it. To fix the buttermilk dilemma some reviews have mentioned, try this: to make substitute buttermilk, add 1-3/4 tablespoons of cream of tartar to a cup of milk, or add a tablespoon of lemon juice or white vinegar to a cup of milk and let it stand for 5 to 10 minutes. In many baking recipes, you can also just use plain yogurt or sour cream instead of buttermilk. I use the vinegar method but the rest are good to know. I never buy buttermilk anymore because I never use the whole carton. Buttermilk is one of those where I could have it for weeks then not need it, as soon as it goes bad I need it. This is handy to keep in your box for any recipe calling for buttermilk, when in a pinch use a substitute.

text:
This is the best recipe I've found for chicken fried steak!  I allow my steaks to "rest" on a wire rack after the final coating of flour - which seems to help the coating adhere - also make sure to pat your steaks dry with paper towels then season them as you'd like before beginning the breading process -  this will also help the coating adhere better.  It is also important that the oil reach the proper temperature before adding the steaks - I used Mazola Canola oil instead of shortening and did not need near the amount called for - used maybe 3/4 - 1c total.  After the steaks are cooked and keeping warm (to prevent sogginess keep them on a wire rack over a cookie sheet) in a 200 oven; I do add some finely chopped onion and garlic to the oil and drippings in the pan and saute before adding the flour and milk - make sure the flour is cooked in the oil to avoid a pasty, flour-y taste to your gravy.  I also like to add about 1/4c chicken stock after adding the milk - I found I only needed about 2 1/2 to 3c of milk.  These additions seem to give the gravy the boost my family likes.  An EXCELLENT recipe that my family loves, thanks so much for sharing!

text:
My middle son loves chicken fried steak and so do I. He came back for seconds with this recipe. I had to change it a little. Because I'm in the Denver area, frying can be a problem - things get overdone on the outside while undercooked inside. So as soon as the outsides were done, I put them in the oven like shake-and-bake for about 1/2 hour. Also, IMHO, a touch of garlic immensely improves country gravy, so I added garlic powder to the gravy. I also couldn't find uncultured buttermilk, but regular milk worked fine.

text:
Followed the recipe with everything except 3 cups of shortening for frying.  I used 1 stick of shortening and 1/2 cup of vegetable oil.  I let my oil stay too hot and the bits and flour got too dark in the bottom of the pan, ill have to monitor the temp a little better next time.  I seasoned the steaks on both sides with salt and pepper prior to pounding out.  I placed steaks between 2 pieces of plastic wrap, and kept the mallot clean.  
I love the idea of using buttermilk and hot sauce in the egg mixture, I think that Ill cut back a tad bit on the hot sauce though next time.  I never buy buttermilk..for every 1 cup of buttermilk needed; I replace 2 tablespoons of regular milk with 2 tablespoons of white vinegar or lemon juice and let sit for 5 minutes to sour. I didnt have a problem with the breading coming off of the meat, a few of the tricks to preventing this is to make sure the oil is hot enoug as well as have the steaks at room temperature when breading and frying.  This is to prevent too much rapid shrinkage.  If the cubed steaks are very cold when breaded and frying, the meat will shrink very fast leaving gaps between the fried breading and the meat causing the breading to come off more easy.  Also only flip the steaks ONCE!! resist the urge to keep flipping back and forth! Too much flipping will cause the breading to loosen and come off. Next time Ill only make half the recipe for gravy, as written it makes way too much for just 4 servings. Great recipe! Keeper!

text:
My first time making this sort of thing and faired pretty well.  I am, however, glad that I refered also to my bible, "Joy of Cooking," and decided to let the battered & floured steaks rest/dry out on a wire rack for 15 min. before frying.  This made the batter stick much better.  I used vegetable oil instead of solid shortening and fried them in a heavy nonstick skillet as I do not have a cast iron one.   I served these with mashed potatoes, 
"Kickin' Collard Greens," also from this site, and buttermilk biscuits.  All in all, a successful first effort for a Yankee.

I previously stayed away from trying to cook this and opted to purchase chicken fried steak from restaurants. Well, not anymore. One of the best breading recipes I have come across for chicken fried steak. The crust was crispy and seasoned and I even got the gravy right.  Tip to everyone saying that it is bland... one of the first lessons of frying anything is to season the meat first. Otherwise, you have seasoned breading with tasteless meat. text:
The spice mix was good (although I added a few more not listed).  The crunch was good, but the coating was thin.  I am amazed at the readers uploaded pictures.  How did you get the batter to stay on like that?  My pieces looked beautiful, until I turned them over and the coating fell off.  This batter just doesnt stick when you cut into the meat either.  I found the combination of baking soda and baking powder strange.  When you add the liquid you have a chemical reaction go off.  Also when you dip the steak after the first coating of flour all the flour you just had on it disappears into the liquid.  I am also not convinced that the pepper, salt and spices should go in the liquid mix since it sinks to the bottom and misses the chance to spice up the steak.  I just really want the flavor and texture of a good old chicken fried steak and sadly this doesnt cut it.  By the end I even tried making a thick paste by mixing the flour in with the liquid.  The batter seemed to stick better and it definitely had more spices coating it.  I will try this recipe again until I find the answer to a better sticking batter.

text:
This recipe definitely is a home run! One thing I have to mention is that the recipe makes enough for at least 6 steaks, so you may want to adjust accordingly. I added 1 tsp. of poultry seasoning to give it the authentic "chicken" flavor. As a substitute for buttermilk, I whisked 3/4 cup sour cream with 3/4 cup milk and it worked great. I didn't put the spices in with the milk & egg. I mixed them with the flour so that when I used the flour for the gravy, it was seasoned. It also wasn't necessary to use so much shortening. I started with 1 cup and added an additional 1/2 cup as I cooked the steaks. This is a wonderful recipe - hope this helps!

text:
A very good and tasty recipe. To boost flavor, instead of salt in the flour mix I use Morton Season All seasoned salt, and 2 tbs. A good way to make the flour to stick to the batter: instead of patting the flour onto the steak, press very firmly with your palm, rocking sideways and forward/back. I normally start with a good portion of the flour mix to the side. I put the battered steak in the main mix then pour the flour to the side over it then start pressing, then flip and repeat.

text:
I would have given this all 5 stars for crispiness alone! If you like flavor, you'll have to kick it up a notch or 2. Easy enough! I recommend adding MORE pepper, salt, garlic and pepper sauce! Next time I make this, and there will be a next time, I will double all the seasonings. Also, since you'll have extra milk mixture, mix it with your leftover flour, 1/2 cup of cornmeal and 1 tablespoon of onion powder. Then drop by the spoonful into the hot oil. My twins called them cornballs, I called them corn fritters. Either way it makes a really nice addition to this Southern style meal!

text:
Great chicken fried steak recipe.  I have tried to make this numerous times and I was finally staisfied with the breading.  My wife and I have lived here in Fort worth for nearly a year now and if there is one dish I have learned that is Texan it is chicken fried steak.  This recipe is sure to satisfy any true texans out there I'm sure.  Only change I made was omitting the hot sauce, substituting 1 1/4 cp milk and 1/4 cp vinegar for buttermilk and using garlic salt instead of real galrlic.  It still turned out awesome, oh yeah and I only needed 3 cups of milk for the gravy,  This was just for my wife and I and we still had plenty left over.

text:
The only two problems' I see is when the steak is done do not tent with foil this will cause the breading to separate from the meat and also get soggy that is because of the steam that gets trapped under the foil dry on a paper towel then place on a wire rack in a 300 degree oven till all is done now the gravy I have seen another comment saying let the flour brown before adding the milk to cook the flour taste out no add the milk and cook for 10 to 15 minutes that will do the trick this is a white pepper gravy not a base for Gumbo please don't be offended I am only giving constructive criticism the recipe still gets 5 Stars in my book keep up the great work

text:
This is the first time I've made chicken fried steak and I'm very pleased, as my husband LOVED it!  He is "beyond" picky so I'm very happy when I find something that he really likes.  

I had 6 cube steaks that made up two pounds and I did pound them very thin, so that may be why I needed to use considerably more flour for the coating.  It seemed that the batter really soaked up the flour and made it necessary to add more.  I did use up almost all the batter to coat the six steaks.

I also used vegetable oil instead of shortening, as that was what I had on hand.  Not one bit of the coating came off.  I think the secret to keeping the coating intact is to use enough oil or shortening and have it at the right temperature, not too hot or too cold.  I used "light" buttermilk, as that was all the store had.  

I don't have a cast iron skillet large enough, so I used my large copper core All-Clad saute pan and it worked just fine.

The Tabasco sauce didn't make it hot, just added a mild "bite", which was offset by the creamy gravy.

This recipe took me longer to put together than anticipated, but it was worth the effort.  I would recommend it to anyone who is looking for a recipe that is likely to please most everyone.  This is a great recipe!

text:
This was a fantastic recipe!!  I pretty much followed it to the T as I always do the first time around.  Things I will change or be sure to do next time: Season the meat as well, if you get a bite without a lot of batter it is rather bland. Be sure the meat is TOTALLY dry before coating or it won't stick as well. Also, I'm at a slightly higher altitude (Denver area) and I did find that it browned rather quickly in the oil without cooking the meat thoroughly. I pulled it out of the pan once browned and placed in the over for approx. 7 min at 375 degrees and it was perfect. I used buttermilk in the gravy too which I wouldn't necessarily suggest, it made it a little too sweet. All around great recipe though!  Thanks for sharing, I'll deffinitely be making this again.

text:
We prepared this Chicken Fried Steak tonight. Being a Texan, trust me I know a thing or two about Chicken Fried Steak, and this was absolutely one of the best I have ever eaten!  Couple things to note... - To get a little more flavor, season the bare meat with some salt and pepper before flouring and dredging it.  - We found medium-low heat to be just about perfect for cooking. Let each side cook roughly 5 minutes and the steak was cooked perfectly. But I think even without that stuff, this recipe is fantastic! Good luck, and enjoy it!

text:
This turned out great! I love this meal in restaurants, but I've never ventured to make chicken fried steak myself before. The breading came out terrific and the flavor was awesome! I didn't use tobasco, but I did put chili powder in both the milk wash and the flour mix--I also used a lot more spices (like double, at least). I loved the tips about letting the battered meat "rest" before cooking, as it really did insure that the breading stuck. I bought round steak and had the butcher run it thru the tenderizer (cheaper thn buying the cube steak) and then I tenderized it a bit more before breading it. I cheated a little by using store-bought country gravy mix, but I did add some of the milk & flour mixtures when cooking it to increase the amount.  Hubby said to add this to the list of "regulars" so that means it's a winner!

text:
This was really good!  The directions were clear. The crust on the steaks turned out nice and crispy and the steaks were done perfectly at 3 1/2 min per side.   Sour cream was used in place of the buttermilk (3/4 c sour cream + 1/4 c water for each cup of buttermilk).  That batter really does the trick!    Next time I might kick the spices up a little and use butter instead of the leftover oil for the gravy.  Thank you for sharing!
By special request for my sons birthday, I made this again.  The hot sauce and garlic were doubled and buttermilk was used this time in the breading.  When the steaks came out of the fry oil, they were dusted on both sides with salt & pepper.  For the gravy, all the oil was poured off, saving the crusty bits in the pan and then a 1/4 c salted butter was substituted in place of the reserved oil.  Once the gravy was mostly done,  garlic and several good shakes of hot sauce were added with the salt and pepper.  Yummy!  This recipe is an excellent starting point and you can be flexible with the spices, adjusting it to your taste.

Amazing. Simply the best fried steak I have ever made. My mother in law was raised on a farm by a woman who refused to cook on anything other than a wood stove until she died in the 80s. I find it has better flavor is I use a cream gravy mix in place of the flour. We use reserve tobasco, which has a smoother flavor.

As always, skillet chicken fried steak is a lot of work but it was a good recipe!!  I never have buttermilk and always to the 1 tbls of white vinegar and fill the rest of the 1 cup up with milk...and I had more than half of the 'buttermilk' left over. Really an en excellent recipe! It was a "feel good" comfort food that evoked a lot of great memories for my wife and I and our time in Oklahoma. I agree with one of the other reviewers that salt and peppering the meat first may enhance the flavor. This was a big hit tonight at our house and fun to make. I highly recommend it served with mashed potatoes and a veggie on the side. This is the chicken fried steak recipe I will use from now on. After I was through I put some red pepper and a little sugar in the batter and fried up some flattened chicken breast for spicy chicken sandwiches and they were really great.

text:
So yummy! I followed the directions exactly, other than seasoning the cube steaks before dredging in flour. The flavor of both the Chicken Fried Steaks and the gravy were right on for my family. I was hesitant to use the Tabasco in the batter, but I'm glad I did. It's not enough to add heat (my kids would not eat it if it were spicy), just flavor. I do think that the recipe takes quite a bit longer than 40 minutes, but I cooked 6 steaks, mashed potatoes, gravy and corn on the cob in about an hour and a half. This is an occasional indulgence for us, and I will definitely use this recipe again next time! Thanks Norah!!!

text:
I used Gluten Free flour and left out the hot sauce.  I bought the powered buttermilk that someone mentioned here and added it to the dry ingredients first before adding the liquid portion of the batter.  This recipe was enough to make 6 large cubed steaks (3-4 lb. total) and still had batter left over.  The coating came off the first steak; possibly didn't have the oil heated high enough.  The rest of the steaks came out perfectly with a nice thick crust. I had never used baking soda & powder and the double dip method to fry foods before. Tasted just as good as restaurant versions I've order. The gravy came out perfect too.

text:
This recipe may be a little TOO good. I just had to thaw out some cube steaks in the microwave and make this for myself at 10PM because I had a craving and nothing else sounded nearly as satisfying for my late dinner. This always comes out perfect -- steaks are flavorful, crispy on the outside and tender on the inside. The only changes I make to this are to use garlic powder instead of minced garlic, double the Tabasco sauce in the batter, and lightly season the steaks with salt and pepper after frying them. Thank you for posting this; it's the only recipe I'll use for chicken-fried steak from now on.

text:
Oh, my!!!  I have gotten many great recipes from this site, and this rates more than 5 stars!!  
Left out the hot sauce, seasoned the dredging flour with Roast Beef Seasoning and fresh ground black pepper.  Didn't have buttermilk-never gets used fast enough.  So..........I borrowed another cook's hint for a substitute and whisked together 2% milk and cream of tartar.  Let it sit for about 10 minutes, whisked again, and viola!!!  Buttermilk!
My husband goes bananas over chicken fried steak, and I think I would have a mutiny on my hands if I made it any other way, after tonight!!
When I asked on a 1-10 scale, with 1 being "ewwwww! and 10 being "I would eat the leftovers for breakfast in the morning"  He says "You kidding?  I'm gonna eat the leftovers cold later for a midnight snack".  I think he liked it!  Thank you so much for sharing this one with us, Norah!  "You done good!!!"

I was skeptical when trying this but it turned out great! It was easy to make. I have an electric stove; the key was to not allow your grease to get too hot! I kept mine on medium heat to allow the meat to cook throughly. The breading was crispy and tasted just like the restuarants. Two lbs of meat was too much= to 6 steaks (we only needed 4) and when you tenderize the meat to 1/4" the steaks are huge; enough for 2 people. Next time I will only make 2 steaks and half the recipe. I was not comfortable making the gravy from this recipe since it did not give an exact amount of flour so I used a country gravy also found on this site

country:

text:
Perfect recipe.  I used 1/2 cup of buttermilk as one and a half seemed a bit much and I make my own.  Didn't want to waste.  I also drained the oil out of the frying pan and used just fresh flour to retain that white gravy color. Breading on chicken fried steak should be like an entity to itself with a different texture and flavor than the steak it houses.  This hit the mark.  The tabasco added a tang that I enjoyed and fresh garlic is always welcome in my home. A tip, when flouring the meat, take the time to work it into the pores of the meat by pressing down on it before you fry and you will keep your breading.  Also, use hot oil on medium or the flour will soak it up and the steaks will be soggy. I made CFS for a living when I was a teenager, and this is the best recipe I have seen in 15 years.

text:
I grew up in Texas, where we knew our way around a chicken fried steak. I never had the temerity to cook one, but I sure knew a good one when I found it.   My nephew is a displaced Californian, whose every other word is "upscale", "fine dining" "balsamic vinegar", "Havarti cheese" and other assorted trendy catchphrases.  My husband is a former hippy vegan from Oregon.  Neither of them ever liked good Southern style cooking; they always had a criticism of anything I ever cooked besides chicken stirfry.   So imagine my surprise when they clamored that this was one of the best meals they had ever eaten and demanded more!  I think this is the only meal where either ever liked a fried food with a crust.  This one is tender and delicious beyond words and I am so grateful for having found it ! I serve it with homemade mashed potatoes, asparagus, biscuits and a local white pepper gravy mix because i deep fry it rather than pan fry.

text:
This recipe was great and I used the tip from someone else to use 1 tbsp. of white vinegar to milk and let it sit for 10 minutes instead of buttermilk.  Also it says to mix in remaining flour which I did and the gravy was too thick and I had to pour in more milk.  I would slowly add the flour into the hot oil and add just enough to use all of the oil without it getting too thick then pour the milk.  These were outstanding and will make again!

text:
Great recipe.  My husband raved about it hours after eating it.  I added about 5 dashes of Tabasco to the gravy to give it the extra kick that it needed.. and it says season to taste with salt and pepper.. so if yours was bland add more seasonings.. I used about 2 - 3 tsp salt and added about 1 tsp of pepper in addition to the tabasco in the gravy.  It turned out great !! The cast iron skillet is a great tool for this -- Lodge makes a great one around 35 (for large 12 inch size)  Another tip: I used the buttermilk -- the coating got gloppy and next time I will layer the steaks with sheets of wax paper between so the coating does not stick to other steaks as you stack them before frying!  Thanks for the great recipe.

this is pretty much the same as my southern family recipe that i make weekly. the addition of hot sauce is perfect, and i hadn't tried it before. i don't ever add the baking soda or powder, and i am not sure why i would. might try it one day to see the difference i guess. i season it up quite a bit more with salt, pepper and garlic powder. cfs is my husbands favorite, and he wont order it at restaurants because mine is so much better. great great great recipe!!!   OH i also use this for fried chicken breasts (texans call it chicken fried chicken). i just marinate the chicken overnight in buttermilk. make sure the chicken breasts are pounded thin, like the steaks). also after breading let it sit for half an hour so the breading wont fall off. serve it with the gravy. haven't tried it with the hot sauce but i will!

Hi, this is Norah, and I submitted this recipe.  Just to clear up a bit of confusion; the baking powder, baking soda, pepper, and salt are not mixed in with the flour; they're mixed in with the buttermilk to create a loose batter.  Also, the cube steaks ARE lightly seasoned with salt, pepper and garlic powder.  This was specified in my original submission, but for some reason this step was left out when the recipe was finalized.  I'm glad there are so many positive reviews, and hopefully this will end any confusion.  Thank you and I hope you enjoy!!

Absolutely delicious! I read a few reviews, got some good tips. I seasoned the  meat with fresh cracked salt and pepper, and used my meat mallet to lightly pound into my cubed steak. I also let the steaks rest for 15 or 20 minutes before frying, and cut the milk down to 3 cups for the gravy, which a half cup of that I used to mix with flour before adding to pan. I find I get the smoothest gravy doing that, and it does not burn.  End result, one of the most delicious dinners I've ever cooked in my kitchen! I'll definitely be making this often!

country:
None
text:
I'm giving this recipe four stars because it's a good recipe for someone starting out on chicken-fried steak. The fifth star is because, even though I didn't actually USE the complete recipe, I gleaned a couple of tips that prove even an old dog can learn new tricks, and my personal recipe is now perfect.

#1.  I pounded in the salt and pepper. Why didn't *I* think of that? (from a comment).

#2. Momma didn't teach me about using the baking powder and soda in my flour mixture. Wow! That's a game-changer.

Don't go to seed over shortening. If you don't like it, use vegetable oil. Use lard if you want to! The important part is to keep it around 350F when you fry. (Lard? Hey, chicken-fried steak is not health food, so splurge if you prefer that flavor.)

And gee whiz, don't go nuts with the flour. Coat them, give a slight shake, then let them set for a few minutes before frying. If you put globs of flour on them, of course they're going to taste odd.

text:
I made this exactly as the recipe said, except I used good old fashioned lard to fry it in.  It turned out awesome!  First time I've ever made chicken fried steak and the flavor was awesome and it was nice and crispy.  I had one problem though.  When building the coating I had trouble with it getting stuck to the pan in the last step before frying.  When I pressed the flour into the meat, the flour on the bottom side would stick to the pan, so I need to come up with a new method of insuring the coating stays adhered to the meat.

I may just dredge it a third time after it sits 10 min., and put it directly into the pan.

I couldn't imagine making this in anything other than a cast iron pan!

My guest thoroughly enjoyed it as well. Next time (which will be very soon) I will make sure to remember a picture for y'all.

I followed the recipe with out modification. The steaks came out well cooked and tasted fine, a bit chewy but that was the meat, not the recipe.  I made the gravy as directed even if it seemed a bit different from how I generally make from scratch gravy. The gravy broke and was unrecoverable.  I had to start over and make my old standard gravy.  My boys weren't crazy about the meal. My husband was luke warm. I do really like the batter and will use it in the future but not likely for steak. I don't often goof up a recipe, I'm a very seasoned cook. But maybe the gravy was just not ment to be. Thank you for the awesome batter though.

text:
So delicious,! Buttermilk is definitely the secret ingredient for sure, the batter was plenty thick and made enough to do 6 large pieces of steak. however, I wouldnt suggest drying the pieces on the rack like the recipe calls for, because as the meat rest, it tends to loose juices and dries out the steak. Instead, fry in batches, and wait to bread the second batch after you turn the 1st steaks over.

text:
My husband and I are from Texas, so we know chicken fried steak.  This was my first time making it and it turned out really good. The only thing I changed was to lightly season the meat before battering it.  I also got a little distracted while frying them up and let the oil get too hot which scorched the tidbits.  Watch your oil temperature!  I ended up discarding the burnt stuff and made my gravy without them.  To compensate for my mistake, I added a little beef bullion, garlic and onion powder. Disclosure... I followed the recipe exactly with the exception of highly seasoning the meat before I dredged it in the flour. I also used cubed steak so I did not have to pound it.

Ive made chicken fried steak for years & my family has loved it. I dont even remember where or how I got the recipe I used. But, when this recipe came to my email, I read the recipe & the rave reviews, & decided I should at least give it a try. I chose to do that when our son was visiting us from Texas. CFS is one of his favorites & I knew I was at high risk by changing up the recipe. (Probably not a wise move. ??) I tried to pull a fast one & did not tell my husband or son that it was a new recipe. However, they noticed immediately. Boy, was I relieved when the CFS was declared delicious AND better tasting than my old, original recipe. Whew! So... out with the old & in with the new.

I also followed one reviewers gravy recipe by sauting onions & garlic, stirring in the flour, cooking a few minutes & adding the milk/cream followed by chicken stock. The gravy was outstanding as well.

text:
Ive made this recipe twice, following directions both times, and both times my family and I found that both steak and breading were tasteless, yet so rich from the frying that none of us could eat more than half. Plus, the clean-up was a major chore. The patties I used were pretty thin, but maybe they should have been thinner. If I were to make it again - which I wont, but if I did - I would 1)pound the heck out of the meat; 2) salt and pepper the meat prior to breading it; 3) add a lot more salt and pepper to the breading, and possibly more tabasco; 4) jazz up the gravy with garlic salt and a few other things as suggested by other reviewers; and 5) use less than half of the recommended oil. Giving it two stars because of all the changes that need to be made, and the fact that both cooking and clean-up were too much work for a meal we couldnt eat.

text:
Black pepper MAKES THE DIFFERENCE!  I recommend about three times as much and rough grind it fresh.  Tabasco hot sauce is several times as potent as most other hot sauces though the pepper mash for a great many of them is purchased from the McKilhenny Corp. and diluted much more.  While South Louisiana natives may find this recipe mild, folks from the rest of the nation may not be accustomed to hardly any spice and may be overwhelmed by it.  I have traveled over a good bit of the nation and have learned this by experience.

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
This is the best recipe I've found for breaking the steak. You definitely need to do the double, if not, triple dredge. I don't measure the hot sauce in the wet ingredients but know I triple or quad it. I also add more black pepper to the dry and 1/4 tsp of cayenne. This recipe is also very good for fried chicken. I add granulated garlic, onion powder, black pepper, and Lawreys season salt to the meat before pounding it. I use a needle tenderizer which pushes the seasonings into the meat. This addition definitely adds more flavor to the dish. We use pork tenderloin (cheaper than beef) most of the time. I guess you could call it redneck schnitzel. The keys to the breaking are the buttermilk, baking soda, and baking powder.. For future meals, we dredge everything and freeze the cutlets on a cutting board and then seal them. Take them out the night before fore breakfasts or for dinner that night. Thank you for putting this recipe on the site, it is my goto fried steak recipe!

I have a little unorthodox Texas twist on chicken-fried steak (CFS).  Im a single guy who buys a big chuck roast, splits it in two, freezes one half and cuts 1 inch off for the CFS.  That slice requires beating w/ the dull side of a big knife in a zip bag.  But, first add the flour, a little corn starch to make it crispy, pinches of white pepper, salt, paprika, onion powder, garlic powder, etc.  Only THEN, beat it into softness with your cleavers dull edge.  Because the coatings are beaten into the meats exterior, they stick and infuse better.  No caking egg required.

This is fabulous!! I made this for my elderly mother, chicken fried steak is one of her favorites, she raved over this recipe.  The only changes I made is I substituted creama con sol (mexican sour cream that is thinner consistency than regular sour cream) instead of using the buttermilk because I don't readily have it on hand. I highly recommend trying it, if you haven't already.  This will be going into my "family favorites" recipe file.  YUM!!

text:
I enjoy the bare bones of this batter recipe, I use it for chicken and pork as well but to add a little more umph I season the flour with paprika, black pepper, kosher salt, onion powder, and garlic power  - to sight (I don't have any measurements yet, but like to be able to see the seasoning in the flour) when I use it for  chicken. when making pork I substitute  paprika for seasoned salt.  I also make my own buttermilk by adding a tablespoon and a half to the measuring cup BEFORE measuring out the milk - letting it sit for at least five minutes before use. I also prefer to make my own shortening as well by using 2 cups of vegetable oil and 2 cups of butter, because I don't really use shortening... Also instead of using Tabasco I use Louisiana hot sauce. So basically I altered this recipe enough for it to be considered a different one entirely, but I do follow the batter instructions to a T - just thought I'd share my version :)

text:
This was ok, but way too involved. When you get your steaks, ask the butcher to run them through the tenderizer once. Save yourself some time. You don't need baking powder or soda.  The tabasco is a nice touch. However, I would discourage using the "leftover" flour to make your gravy. Two reasons, one, with the egg and such, it's more likely to make lumpy gravy. And secondly, you've got raw pieces of meat in there that won't fully get cooked.  I would suggest using fresh flour, equal parts flour to oil. Brown your flour. Then  add your milk. :)  It's nice to try new versions of my favorite meal. Thank you. :)

So this is the second time that have made this recipe and I tried a few changes if your interested. First I used ground chicken this time instead of cube steak. Since ground chicken is so mild and moist, I added a half of cup of panko and 1 T each of Worchester sauce and soy sauce. I stayed true to the rest of the recipe and they turned out great! text:
The 1st two that I fried were a disaster. Followed the recipe exactly, but coating came completely off in the pan. I searched the reviews frantically for help. Thank you EKERR19 for this recipe saving tip!: rub salt & pepper on the steaks before dredging. After dredging, let them sit for a couple of minutes on a wire rack before frying. The rest of the steaks came out beautifully using this tip. I fried in an electric skillet, 5 min per side, then transferred to a cast iron to make the gravy. Delicious, & so tender! Made it for my parents, & they loved it! Served with mashed potatoes & "Grandma's Baking Powder Biscuits". Success!

This recipe was pretty good. I have never had chicken fried steak before and was amazed at how much it looked like fried chicken . The only suggestion I might make (like many others) is to season the steak with salt and pepper before the initial dip in the flour. Also I substituted the shortening for plain old vegitable oil. If you are a lover of well seasoned dishes you might also want to add an extra dash of salt and pepper to the flour and the buttermilk batter as well. **please note that the gravy in my picture is not the one in this recipe.

text:
I am giving this 4 stars as I did make some changes due to the reviews. 

First I seasoned the steaks with salt, garlic powder and pepper.  I also used the same seasoning combo in the flour.  No measurements I just shake some in mix it up and smell.  I also added more hot sauce the "batter" was orangeish.  

Second, I didn't use crisco, I used vegetable oil.  

Third, I was not NOT wasting 4 cups of milk (milk is expensive) for gravy.  That's ridiculous, I used 2 cups milk and a pouch of brown gravy mix as well as a little oil from the bottom of the pan.  added pepper.  

This was a huge hit.  My husband wants it in the rotation, it didn't take long to make, my 17 month old daughter was a "clean plater" and wanted seconds.  I loved the flavor and crunch, and liked the gravy very much, w/o the modifiations the gravy would have been bland.  

My husband did request that I make country gravy next time just because he likes country gravy.

text:
I made this recipe gluten-free and dairy-free and LOVED IT!  I replaced the flour with Bob's Red Mill all-purpose gluten-free flour, replaced the buttermilk with soy milk and a tablespoon of lemon juice, and replaced the milk in the gravy with rice milk.  (Soy milk is a little too sweet for gravy.)  I added garlic to everything, because in my house, you can't ever have too much garlic, and I took the advise of others and seasoned the meat before coating.  I also used half chicken and half cube steak. (Pound out the chicken, too!)  The chicken was just as good, maybe better?  (And now I know I can do allergy-free fried chicken!)  Next time, I will season the batter a litte more, too, with more salt, pepper, and of course, garlic.  Overall, this recipe is AMAZING, and it was great to have chicken fried steak and chicken once again, after years of missing out due to allergies.  Also, the other 3 "non-allergics" in the house said it was definitely a keeper!  We all cleaned our plates!  Thanks for this one!!

text:
First off; 2 cups of flour was a waste of a cup of flour. Keep the other dry ingredients the same, but don't throw away a cup of flour. 
Second; I pre-seasoned the meat with salt & pepper, and glad I did, it gave the meat just a enough extra flavor.
3rd: I used lard instead of the shortening, liked the boost it gave to the meat.
Lastly: The gravy was very bland, although the lard helped it. I added Tabasco (1/2 teas.), a teaspoon of Worcestershire sauce, and additional salt & pepper to the gravy. 
The meat, the dredge & batter was very good and help up well. I was impressed with that, but again, the gravy really needed some work.
I would make this again with the changes I made.

text:
Excellent recipe!  Made a couple changes, personal preference.  I used milk instead of buttermilk, to cut out some fat, and added a couple tablespoons of flour to thicken batter.  And I made a sausage gravy.  I browned country sausage in a sauce pan, removed sausage.  Added some extra oil, heated, added flour to make a blond roux.  Added hot milk, sausage and salt and pepper.  Look at "Super Sausage Gravy" for a good method for making the gravy.

This was a great recipe.  I have never used crisco to fry and was a little wary but these fried perfectly. however - my stove is not thanking me that much for this recipe with all the oil :) I used seven 1/2 pound beef cubes so I pretty much doubled the recipe.  I thought the eight cups if flour was a little much for the gravy and i had to add a boatload of seasoning (garlic powder, onion pepper, cayenne pepper, hotsauce) to try to tame down the floury taste.  Next time i will keep the flour the same at four cups no matter the quantity.  Also, i asked the people i was serving what they would do differently next time and they said that while it was flavourful, i should season the meat prefry.  Great dinner all in all.  I served it with garlic mashed potatoes and collard greens

text:
My California in-laws had never eaten CFS before, and they went nuts over these. I'm not a gravy fan, so I didn't make a gravy for them, and nobody missed not having one. Followed the recipe except I deep fried the coated cube steak in lard at 375F. On smaller steaks (say 3 ounce pieces or less) the coating always stays intact and the meat comes out perfect - amazingly moist and tender for cube steak. The Tabasco gives it a nice pepper flavor without being too strong. Oil absorption is miminal. Nephew can't wait for me to return and cook these again.

text:
Great tasting chicken fried steak. I gave it 4 stars because I changed it just a bit.  As a few other reviewers mentioned, tastes better to season meat beforehand. A little Lowery's seasoned salt and pepper is perfect.  Then -  didn't need to add any additional salt.  I used garlic pepper, so didn't add garlic cloves.  Used Wesson Oil instead of shortening.  Noticed a few people mentioning that their steak was greasy.   Make sure grease is good and hot before putting meat in there.   I had my grease too hot at first and the grease splattered everywhere.  I turned heat to medium,the splattering stopped, and the meat cooked perfectly. Drained cooked meat on paper towels, and it was great! Meat is tender, and crust is yummy.
